<review>My first visit was on the night of my twins' graduation from HS. We didn't get outta the school till almost 830, so our usual sushi place didnt have enough space for us. We called a few places, and Toshi was the only place that had enough space for our group of 10.

Parking was easy, place was easily spotted. We took up about half the floor space. They let us know immediately that they didnt serve alcohol, but we could bring our own (the 7Eleven next door must love that). It took maybe 10 minutes for our orders to start flying to the table. Each plate was gorgeous. Toshi was humming and cutting, shredding and rolling, and smiling. It is obvious how much he loves his work.

Everyone was very happy with the food. There were audible moans from happy mouths, and everyone was sharing and saying "oh my Yum, you HAVE to try this". Tempura, eel, ripe avocados, perfectly broiled dynamite, melty melty salmon, super fresh albacore drizzled with ponzu on a hand grated mound of daikon dotted with crispy slivered onion.....

Second visit was last night, just me and my man. So so good! Toshi seated us, reminded us about alcohol, and told us the special was local albacore that he was delighted to find earlier that day. Service was perfectly timed, each plate presented right as the previous was done, each visually beautiful and heavenly on the tongue.

We both left pleasantly satiated and dreamily satisfied. And giggly because Toshi hummed something that sounded a lot like Hey there Delilah. üòÇüòÇüòÇ Also, his spanish puts mine to shame.

His food is not just comforting, its art. Highest recommendation!<//review>< Pictures>

<Review>What a small world. I had gone quite often to Toshi's restaurant in Silverlake on Hyperion right next to the Say Cheese store. In fact, I first met Toshi when he was working as Sushi chef at the long gone Zen restaurant also on Hyperion in the early 1990's.

I missed going to Toshi's when he was on Ventura  Blvd, but have accidently but pleasantly met up with him in his North Hollywood/Valley Glen "hidden gem" on Van Owen.

This is a down home, informal, kick back place. There is no classic Kappo-/haute cuisine formality nor ritual. You can scarf down on rainbow, caterpillar, dragon rolls, but Toshi can change gears to a more authentic Edoma√® (eh doh mah eh)/traditional Tokyo style Sushi at the drop of a hat.

I tend to be a Sushi purist so I asked Toshi to facilitate mostly Nigiri (nee ghee ree)/hand shaped Sushi rice w/ seafood on top or a Temaki/classic handroll without mayonnaise, sweet "eel sauce", or non-traditional sriracha garlic chile sauce on every order.

Toshi pulled out good quality:

1) Engawa/halibut fin muscle that was pleasantly chewy w/ a bit of fattiness. Green onion, Shiso/Japanese Basil.

2) Hiram√®/halibut whIch had a bit of sweet sea Umami w/ touch of Yuzu Kosho-/pur√©ed Japanese citrus zest & green chile. Green onion & julienned cucumber.

3) Hotat√® (hoh tah teh)/scallop Temaki/handroll was off white creamy, soft, velvety, plush w/ ocean kissed sweetness. Masago orange fish roe was a nice colour contrast as well as upping the sweet Umami.

4) Ika/squid: flat sheet of pearly white scored to cut fibres in order to soften the meat w/ underlying emerald green Shiso.

Toshi also thoughtfully added small steamed whole baby octopus to include octopod as well was decapod offerings.

5)  Chu-Toro: medium fatty Hon Maguro/bluefin tuna was meaty, soft, fatty, bit beefy. Wasabi & Sho-yu/soy sauce to accentuate the meaty, beefiness.

Green Kaiwar√® Daikon sprouts on the side added a peppery vegetal tone as well as a contrasting green & white to the pink rose colored dawn of the Chu-Toro.

6)  Shiro Maguro/albacore: soft, sensuously soft,.pillowy, lightly sweet meat. Bit of funky green onion & crispy fried sweet onion.

7) Lastly, dessert: Temaki of  sweet Unagi/fresh water eel baked w/ a hint of sweet Sho-yu eel sauce. Slice of oily Aguacate/avocado, green onion, Kaiwar√® Daikon.

1-7a) Brought my own premium Sak√®  (sah keh), Katsuyama Akatsuki Junmai Daiginjo from Sendai City  Miyagi Prefecture.  Scents & tastes of fully ripened summer Japanese pears, bit of honey dew, touch peppery, mildly acidic, smooth, silky, coolness. Nice refined, elegant pairing to the overall meal.

You can bring your own bottle of  Sak√® , wine, beer, and also bring your own crystal for Sak√® or wine since Toshi doesn't have a big selection of appropriate glasses in order to appreciate them.

Toshi pulled out some magical Sushi tricks to allow me to experience a more pure Japanese Edoma√® style which is probably not the typical  way his usual customers order.

Really enjoyed his skill at creating Washoku/classic Japanese cuisine at a moment's notice without any prior warning. 4 Yelp stars for going out of his way to cater to a Sushi purist.<//Review>< GmapID>

<userid>107506492474395347251< /userid>< Rate>
3</Rate>
<time>1540199325236<//time>< text>
At $85 a night, in Los Angeles... I cannot complain too much. If you are hoping for a ground floor room, make a reservation well in advance. It is a 3 story complex without an elevator. I am disabled with a pacemaker, artifical heart valve and a bad knee and I had a little trouble traversing the stairs. Perhaps I should have paid extra for the climbing gear and the Sherpa.

Cosmetically, room 302 it is not the greatest in the world. I pulled the top drawer of the dresser and the top of the dresser and top drawer collapsed into itself. I did my best to piece it back together, sorry about the chincey repair job. After that experience, I took pictures of the damage in the room for fear that the motel may attempt to charge me for the previous damage repairs. There were several paint chips on the walls, one night stand, one bedside light that worked, one chair and a dresser that was once used as target practice by The L.A.P.D.

On to the good stuff! The bed was clean, as were the towels. The bathtub was large enough and clean enough to host a bubble bath. The room came with a refridgerator and a microwave that worked well. The tv worked, yet there are limited basic package channels.

Sidebar: Be careful with the TV remote as the battery cover is missing. Additionally, the condition of the remote could be categorized as sanitary for Skid Row, L.A. Seriously,... I am sure I could have collected 100 DNA samples with the end of a toothpick from in between the buttons. I opted to use a zip lock bag to store the remote in, otherwise make a call to the CDC (Center for Disease Control) and get yourself checked out. Subsequently, I had to pour 1 pound of salt on the zip lock bag and burn it Supernatural style for fear that I may be followed by demons later.

Other than that... the room was fine. Oh, another positive note: The Shower/Bath seems to have a continuous flow hot water heater and it does get "Hot",... be careful. I had warmth for days,... and the water pressure was good as well. The wall mounted air conditioning worked well, but as the air blew, the drapes would blow outward and cover the vents. So the windows were nice and comfortable, but the room would have been hot. To Jerry-rig this problem, I trapped the bottom of the drapes with my shoe on top of the air conditioner,... problem solved.

The view of the neighborhood from the 3rd floor was great, but stay off of the sidewalk after dark unless you have your own Level III Kevlar vest. The staff were nice and the parking area has a CCTV video surveillance system, so your ride will be safe. If you like camping with a TV, this is about two steps up. If you are creeped out by rooms that look like they have been rode hard and put away wet... maybe spend an extra $40 down the street.</text>

< Review>
Really solid Thai place in Berkeley. Fast service and good food! It can get really crowded for dinner on weekends so come before the rush (before 6pm).

Their Tom Yum soup is delicious! The bowl was filled with so much chicken (you can choose to get tofu or chicken). Since they use white meat, the chicken was a little dry, but other than that, soup is perfect!

Tried their duck rice plate. The duck was really tender and drenched in sauce. I wish they put a little less sauce because the sauce itself was overpowering and salty, but if you eat the duck and rice together it was fine.

Pad kee mao is flavorful and just the right amount of spiciness to it! Filled with veggies and lots of noodles, this was my favorite dish of the night!

Excited to come back and try more dishes (although finding parking is such a pain because well... it's Berkeley).< /Review>

<user>115694123052356676215<//user>< name>
Alexander Ang-Angco</name>
<date>1510692753542</date><Rate>4<//Rate>< text>
Reviewing for a ToGo experience: easy to call in (challenging to find a reliable menu online), food was made fast and payment was easy. For the record: ordering to go is never the same experience as eating in- the food can suffer and the presentation can foul your appetite. Finding a restaurant that can still keep that charm between ToGo and Eating-In are far and few in-between. Imm Thai has nailed my ToGo expectations. The food is a clear 4/4 stars! Definitely one of the best Thai food menus around downtown Berkeley. The Drunken Noodles were perfect level of heat that woos you in for more but doesn‚Äôt leave your mouth regretting it. With thin slices of chicken with fried tofu, the dish wasn‚Äôt oily or skimpy on the toppings. Green beans were cooked nicely with a slight blistering of char. Portions are about right for the price tag. Would recommend this place to anyone.</text>

<resp>None< /resp>< Review>
Probably the best Thai food in the bay! Their pad see ew is the best I've had outside of Thailand, and everything else we've tried has been delicious as well. Can't go wrong with any of the staples, so trust your gut and order what you usually get at other Thai restaurants and just get ready to have an amazing meal.

It gets crowded at lunch and dinner times so be prepared to wait a bit. Most of the tables are small, so if you go with a larger group (i.e. more than 3), you might get a little frustrated watching a bunch of two tops getting seated before you. But persevere and you'll enjoy some amazing Thai food at super reasonable prices.< /Review>

<Text>The rating is for the food.

I visited this place on a Monday evening a of week ago. Super packed but managed to get a table relatively quickly (15-20 minutes wait). Delicious food, service was only 'okay' due to the number of people. I can't fault them for that, and would have to re-visit during a less busy time to rate the service.

Frankly, one of the best intro's I've had to a Thai restaurant. Everything - and I mean everything - that we as a group tried there was good.
Tom Yum soup (vegan style): 10/10
Pad see ew (w/chicken): 10/10
Fried rolls (Vegan): 10/10
Basil (w/chicken): 8/10 (Note: I don't like green beans, but even I admit this was great)
Red Curry (vegan): 10/10 - sweetly spicy heat that really creeps up on you in a good way.
The Hot Ginger tea was fantastic as well.

Try this place, you won't regret it if you like Thai food.</Text>< Pics>

< text>
Best kind of Thai place. The kitchen is slammed, the wait staff is stretched thin, but the food is fantastic. I recommend the spicy eggplant and the braised pork. Both are so flavourful, and the rice soaks up all the delicious juices. It's also super hot and fresh because they're turning out a ton of volume. My favorite detail is the little tray of picked chilies and chili paste. It was so good. Seemed homemade.

Like I said though, the staff is stretched thin (went on Sunday at dinner). We had someone bring food to our table, and just as I was about to dig in, a different waiter swooped in and took it, telling us it was for someone else. Then they never brought is our drinks, and they were impossible to flag down. It wasn't rude or anything. It just seemed like they were way over worked.

Oh, and on your way in there's actually a sign up sheet behind you, but it looks like people are queued up because the line for take out is right there too. We saw at least four parties make the same mistake as we did; just waiting around for a while before someone would come tell them they had to sign up.</text>

< Pictures>
None</Pictures>
<text>Being on a budget and craving Thai food, a friend and I decided to try Imm Thai since it looked like a broke-college-student-kind-of-budget place to eat. We get there and it's packed for a tiny place; however we were seated right away. We order a plate of wings ($7), a soup ($5), Thai tea ($2.50 each), and we both ordered pad Thai (mine was $8 while my friend's was $12 since she requested tofu, shrimp, and chicken). We first received our wings which was 6 small wings (a little over a dollar each wing) and then we get the soup which was something out of my comfort zone but my friend liked it so I guess it was good. The wings were crispy and drenched in some zing-kind-of sauce. Our teas came which came in 12oz mason jars; it was real Thai leaves they brewed so I gave them that.

The pad Thais came out and it was a lot, and I think it was a lot because after eating the wings and soup I started to become full. The pad Thai was hot, indicator it was made to order, and when I ate it I noticed it tasted almost as good as a place which was completely cheaper. Our waitress was patient and filled up my water cup every time it was low. The service was nice but when the check came out to $40 between the both of us and my friend nearly paid $30 (including tip) it was not a street-food kind of price. Since we split the check I paid $16 (excluding tip) and for one person that was expensive. Yes we ordered what seemed like a lot of food but it wasn't. The soup was small for the expense as well as the wings.

We learned our lesson that Imm Thai Street Food will break the bank. There are of course many other places in Berkeley that will not break the bank. This place can be worth trying but take caution and make sure there's money in your bank account before you proceed. Happy eating!! ^^</text><name>Jazz Baruela< /name><userid>101322665937897630163</userid><time>1427778096848<//time>< rating>

The place is packed! Came here on a Thursdays night. Thankfully we just waited 5 min before getting a table.

The place is kind of cramp, but if that reduces the wait, I can deal with it.

The menu had everything I wanted to taste, ended up with two noodle dish, wanted the poa ki mow, but they ran out of thick noodles but we settle for the thin one, which still tasted delicious.

The Thai coffee was good, the atmosphere was great, they have two big TV showing the game.

Overall, would come back if I'm feeling Thai.< /text>

<rate>3<//rate>< review>
I have to preface this by saying that the  flavors were there and the servers were friendly & patient, but there were many drawbacks to our experience. Firstly, it was so loud we almost left as soon as we were seated. A small amount of acoustic treatment would go a long way here. Even though it was before 7pm, they were out of a number of the appetizers. The "starter" we did end up ordering didn't end up coming out til after we had finished eating the rest and gotten the check, and to add insult to injury it arrived without the requested peanut sauce (which we were charged for). It took 40 minutes to get our first dish (they brought out our entrees about ten minutes apart, super awkward) so the whole experience took over an hour even though we asked for a box & the check the moment the second entree hit the table. We saw "Thai street food" and figured we'd grab a quick curry & noodles, boy were we wrong. I'll give them one more try some other time when I'm not starving and short on time because it was tasty and the servers were nice.< /review>
